No, the `git fetch` command will not overwrite your local files. Here's what `git fetch` does:\\n\\n1. It downloads new data from the remote repository.\\n2. It updates your remote-tracking branches.\\n3. It does not automatically merge or modify your current working directory.\\n\\nIn other words, `git fetch` is a safe operation. It allows you to see what changes exist on the remote without modifying your local files. After fetching, you can review the changes before deciding to merge them into your local branches.\\n\\nIf you want to integrate the fetched changes into your current branch, you would need to explicitly use `git merge` or `git pull` (which is essentially `fetch` + `merge`).\\n\\nSo, you can safely run `git fetch` without worrying about overwriting your local work.
